<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graphics_products_.28discrete_and_AMD_APU_technology.29">Graphics products (discrete and AMD APU technology)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Graphics products (discrete and AMD APU technology)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_AMD_graphics_processing_units" title="List of AMD graphics processing units">List of AMD graphics processing units</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_AMD_Accelerated_Processing_Unit_microprocessors" title="List of AMD Accelerated Processing Unit microprocessors">List of AMD Accelerated Processing Unit microprocessors</a></div>
<p>AMD's portfolio of dedicated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphics_processor" title="Graphics processor">graphics processors</a> as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> includes product families and associated technologies aimed at the consumer, professional and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-performance_computing" title="High-performance computing">high-performance computing</a> markets, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Radeon" title="Radeon">Radeon</a></b> – brand for consumer line of graphics cards; the brand name originated with ATI. <b><a href="/wiki/Radeon" title="Radeon">Mobility Radeon</a></b> offers power-optimized versions of Radeon graphics chips for use in laptops.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/AMD_FirePro" title="AMD FirePro">AMD FirePro</a></b> – brand for professional line of graphics cards for <a href="/wiki/Workstation" title="Workstation">workstations</a>. Succeeds the FireGL series of workstation CAD/CAM video cards, the FireMV series and the AMD FireStream series. Predecessor of the <b>AMD Radeon Pro</b> brand for professional graphics.
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/AMD_FireStream" title="AMD FireStream">AMD FireStream</a></b></i> – brand for <i>discontinued product line</i> targeting <a href="/wiki/Stream_processing" title="Stream processing">stream processing</a> and <a href="/wiki/General-purpose_computing_on_graphics_processing_units" title="General-purpose computing on graphics processing units">GPGPU</a> as used in various industries.</li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/AMD_FireMV" title="AMD FireMV">AMD FireMV</a></b></i> – brand for <i>discontinued product line</i> targeting multi-monitor setups in professional environments.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Radeon_Pro" title="AMD Radeon Pro">AMD Radeon Pro</a></b> - successor to the <b>AMD FirePro</b> brand for workstation graphics cards.
<ul>
<li><i><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Radeon_Pro#Radeon_Pro_WX_Series" title="AMD Radeon Pro">AMD Radeon Pro WX Series</a></b></i> - brand targeting traditional workstation graphics solutions.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> technologies found in AMD products include:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/AMD_Eyefinity" title="AMD Eyefinity">AMD Eyefinity</a></b> – facilitates <a href="/wiki/Multi-monitor" title="Multi-monitor">multi-monitor</a> setup of up to 6 monitors per graphics card</li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_FreeSync" title="AMD FreeSync">AMD FreeSync</a></b> – display synchronization based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VESA" title="VESA">VESA</a> Adaptive Sync standard</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/AMD_TrueAudio" title="AMD TrueAudio">AMD TrueAudio</a></b> – acceleration of audio calculations</li>
<li><b><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=AMD_XConnect&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="AMD XConnect (page does not exist)">AMD XConnect</a></b> - allows the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_GPU" title="External GPU">External GPU</a> enclosures through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thunderbolt_3" title="Thunderbolt 3">Thunderbolt 3</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Unified_Video_Decoder" title="Unified Video Decoder">Unified Video Decoder</a> (UVD)</b> – acceleration of video decoding</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Video_Coding_Engine" title="Video Coding Engine">Video Coding Engine</a> (VCE)</b> – acceleration of video encoding</li>
</ul>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Catalyst" title="AMD Catalyst">AMD Catalyst</a> is a collection of <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary</a> <a href="/wiki/Device_driver" title="Device driver">device driver</a> software available for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>.</p>
<p>Since 2007, AMD has participated in the development of <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_graphics_device_driver" title="Free and open-source graphics device driver">free and open-source graphics device drivers</a>. The programming specifications for a number of chipsets and features were published in several rounds. Employees hired by AMD for this purpose contribute code to the <a href="/wiki/Direct_Rendering_Manager" title="Direct Rendering Manager">Direct Rendering Manager</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AMD_motherboard_chipsets">AMD motherboard chipsets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: AMD motherboard chipsets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comparison_of_AMD_chipsets" title="Comparison of AMD chipsets">Comparison of AMD chipsets</a></div>
<p>Before the launch of <a href="/wiki/Athlon_64" title="Athlon 64">Athlon 64</a> processors in 2003, AMD designed <a href="/wiki/Chipset" title="Chipset">chipsets</a> for their processors spanning the <a href="/wiki/AMD_K6" title="AMD K6">K6</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_K7" title="AMD K7">K7</a> processor generations. The chipsets include the AMD-640, AMD-751 and the AMD-761 chipsets. The situation changed in 2003 with the release of <a href="/wiki/Athlon_64" title="Athlon 64">Athlon 64</a> processors, and AMD chose not to further design its own chipsets for its desktop processors while opening the desktop platform to allow other firms to design chipsets. This was the “<a href="/wiki/Open_Platform_Management_Architecture" title="Open Platform Management Architecture">Open Platform Management Architecture</a>” with <a href="/wiki/ATI_Technologies" title="ATI Technologies">ATI</a>, <a href="/wiki/VIA_Technologies" title="VIA Technologies">VIA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Integrated_Systems" title="Silicon Integrated Systems">SiS</a> developing their own chipset for <a href="/wiki/Athlon_64" title="Athlon 64">Athlon 64</a> processors and later <a href="/wiki/Athlon_64_X2" title="Athlon 64 X2">Athlon 64 X2</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athlon_64_FX" title="Athlon 64 FX">Athlon 64 FX</a> processors, including the <a href="/wiki/AMD_Quad_FX_platform" title="AMD Quad FX platform">Quad FX platform</a> chipset from Nvidia.</p>
<p>The initiative went further with the release of <a href="/wiki/Opteron" title="Opteron">Opteron</a> server processors as AMD stopped the design of server chipsets in 2004 after releasing the AMD-8111 chipset, and again opened the server platform for firms to develop chipsets for Opteron processors. As of today, <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broadcom" title="Broadcom">Broadcom</a> are the sole designing firms of server chipsets for Opteron processors.</p>
<p>As the company completed the acquisition of ATI Technologies in 2006, the firm gained the ATI design team for chipsets which previously designed the <a href="/wiki/Xpress_200" title="Xpress 200">Radeon Xpress 200</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Xpress_3200" title="Xpress 3200">Radeon Xpress 3200</a> chipsets. AMD then renamed the chipsets for AMD processors under AMD branding (for instance, the CrossFire Xpress 3200 chipset was renamed as <a href="/wiki/AMD_580_chipset_series" title="AMD 580 chipset series">AMD 580X CrossFire chipset</a>). In February 2007, AMD announced the first AMD-branded chipset since 2004 with the release of the AMD <a href="/wiki/AMD_690_chipset_series" title="AMD 690 chipset series">690G</a> chipset (previously under the development codename <i>RS690</i>), targeted at mainstream <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Graphics_Processor" title="Integrated Graphics Processor">IGP</a> computing. It was the industry's first to implement a <a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> 1.2 port on motherboards, shipping for more than a million units. While ATI had aimed at releasing an Intel IGP chipset, the plan was scrapped and the inventories of <a href="/wiki/AMD_690_chipset_series#Radeon_Xpress_1250" title="AMD 690 chipset series">Radeon Xpress 1250</a> (codenamed <i>RS600</i>, sold under ATI brand) was sold to two OEMs, Abit and ASRock. Although AMD stated the firm would still produce Intel chipsets, Intel had not granted the license of <span class="nowrap">1333 MHz</span> FSB to ATI.</p>
<p>On November 15, 2007, AMD announced a new chipset series portfolio, the <a href="/wiki/AMD_700_chipset_series" title="AMD 700 chipset series">AMD 7-Series chipsets</a>, covering from enthusiast multi-graphics segment to value IGP segment, to replace the <a href="/wiki/AMD_580_chipset_series" title="AMD 580 chipset series">AMD 480/570/580 chipsets</a> and <a href="/wiki/AMD_690_chipset_series" title="AMD 690 chipset series">AMD 690 series chipsets</a>, marking AMD's first enthusiast multi-graphics chipset. Discrete graphics chipsets were launched on November 15, 2007 as part of the codenamed <i>Spider</i> desktop platform, and IGP chipsets were launched at a later time in spring 2008 as part of the codenamed <i>Cartwheel</i> platform.</p>
<p>AMD returned to the server chipsets market with the <a href="/wiki/AMD_800_chipset_series" title="AMD 800 chipset series">AMD 800S series server chipsets</a>. It includes support for up to six <a href="/wiki/Serial_ATA#SATA_Revision_3.0_.28SATA_6Gb.2Fs.29" title="Serial ATA">SATA 6.0 Gbit/s</a> ports, the C6 power state, which is featured in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Fusion" title="AMD Fusion">Fusion</a> processors and <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Host_Controller_Interface" title="Advanced Host Controller Interface">AHCI</a> 1.2 with SATA <a href="/wiki/Port_multiplier#FIS.28Frame_Information_Structure.29.E2.80.93based_switching" title="Port multiplier">FIS–based switching</a> support. This is a chipset family supporting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phenom_(processor)" title="Phenom (processor)">Phenom</a> processors and <a href="/wiki/AMD_Quad_FX_platform" title="AMD Quad FX platform">Quad FX enthusiast platform</a> (890FX), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Graphics_Processor" title="Integrated Graphics Processor">IGP</a>(890GX).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AMD_Live.21">AMD Live!</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: AMD Live!">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AMD_Live!" title="AMD Live!">AMD Live!</a></div>
<p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, AMD LIVE! was a platform marketing initiative focusing the consumer electronics segment, with an Active TV initiative for streaming Internet videos from web video services such as YouTube, into AMD Live! PC as well as connected digital TVs, together with a scheme for an ecosystem of certified peripherals for the ease of customers to identify peripherals for AMD LIVE! systems for digital home experience, called "AMD LIVE! Ready".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AMD_Quad_FX_platform">AMD Quad FX platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: AMD Quad FX platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AMD_Quad_FX_platform" title="AMD Quad FX platform">AMD Quad FX platform</a></div>
<p>The AMD Quad FX platform, being an extreme enthusiast platform,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> allows two processors to connect through <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a>, which is a similar setup to dual-processor (2P) servers, excluding the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffered_memory" title="Buffered memory">buffered memory</a>/<a href="/wiki/Registered_memory" title="Registered memory">registered memory</a> <a href="/wiki/DIMM" title="DIMM">DIMM</a> modules, and a server motherboard, the current setup includes two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athlon_64_FX" title="Athlon 64 FX">Athlon 64 FX</a>-70 series processors and a special motherboard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> AMD pushed the platform for the surging demands for what AMD calls "megatasking",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> the ability to do more tasks on a single system. The platform refreshes with the introduction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_K10" title="AMD K10">Phenom FX</a> processors and the next-generation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RD700_chipset_series" title="RD700 chipset series">RD790</a> chipset, codenamed "<i>FASN8</i>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Server_platform">Server platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Server platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>AMD's first <a href="/wiki/Symmetric_multiprocessing" title="Symmetric multiprocessing">multi-processor</a> server platform, codenamed <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fiorano_(AMD)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fiorano (AMD) (page does not exist)">Fiorano</a></i>, consists of <a href="/wiki/AMD_800_chipset_series" title="AMD 800 chipset series">AMD SR5690 + SP5100 server chipsets</a>, supporting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/45_nm" title="45 nm">45 nm</a>, codenamed <i>Shanghai</i> <a href="/wiki/Socket_F%2B" title="Socket F+">Socket F+</a> processors and registered DDR2 memory. It was followed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Maranello" title="Maranello">Maranello</a></i> platform supporting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/45_nm" title="45 nm">45 nm</a>, codenamed <i>Istanbul</i>, <a href="/wiki/Socket_G34" title="Socket G34">Socket G34</a> processors with DDR3 memory. On single-processor platform, the codenamed <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalunya" title="Catalunya">Catalunya</a></i> platform consists of codenamed <i>Suzuka</i> 45 nm quad-core processor with <a href="/wiki/AMD_800_chipset_series" title="AMD 800 chipset series">AMD SR5580 + SP5100 chipset</a> and DDR3 support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>AMD's <a href="/wiki/X86_virtualization" title="X86 virtualization">x86 virtualization</a> extension to the 64-bit x86 architecture is named <i>AMD Virtualization</i>, also known by the abbreviation <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD-V" title="AMD-V">AMD-V</a></i>, and is sometimes referred to by the code name "Pacifica". AMD processors using <a href="/wiki/Socket_AM2" title="Socket AM2">Socket AM2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socket_S1" title="Socket S1">Socket S1</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Socket_F" title="Socket F">Socket F</a> include AMD Virtualization support. AMD Virtualization is also supported by release two (8200, 2200 and 1200 series) of the Opteron processors. The third generation (8300 and 2300 series) of <a href="/wiki/Opteron" title="Opteron">Opteron</a> processors will see an update in virtualization technology, specifically the Rapid Virtualization Indexing (also known by the development name <i>Nested Page Tables</i>), alongside the tagged <a href="/wiki/Translation_lookaside_buffer" title="Translation lookaside buffer">TLB</a> and Device Exclusion Vector (DEV).</p>
<p>AMD also promotes the "AMD I/O Virtualization Technology" (also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOMMU" title="IOMMU">IOMMU</a>) for I/O virtualization. The AMD IOMMU specification has been updated to version 1.2. The specification describes the use of a <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a> architecture.</p>
<p>AMD's server initiatives include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>AMD Trinity, provides support for virtualization, security and management. Key features include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD#Virtualization" title="AMD">AMD-V</a> technology, codenamed <i>Presidio</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trusted_computing" title="Trusted computing">trusted computing</a> platform technology, I/O Virtualization and Open Management Partition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>AMD Raiden, future clients similar to the <a href="/wiki/Jack_PC" title="Jack PC">Jack PC</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> to be connected through network to a blade server for central management, to reduce client form factor sizes with AMD Trinity features.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Torrenza" title="Torrenza">Torrenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coprocessor" title="Coprocessor">coprocessors</a> support through interconnects such as <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PCI_Express" title="PCI Express">PCI Express</a> (though more focus was at <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a> enabled coprocessors), also opening processor socket architecture to other manufacturers, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun</a> and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> are among the supporting consortium, with rumoured <a href="/wiki/POWER7" title="POWER7">POWER7</a> processors would be socket-compatible to future Opteron processors. The move made rival <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> respond with the opening of <a href="/wiki/Front-side_bus" title="Front-side bus">front-side bus</a> (FSB) architecture as well as <a href="/wiki/PCI_Express" title="PCI Express">Geneseo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> a collaboration project with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> for coprocessors connected through <a href="/wiki/PCI_Express" title="PCI Express">PCI Express</a>.</li>
<li>Various certified systems programs and platforms: AMD Commercial <a href="/wiki/Stable_Image_Platform" title="Stable Image Platform">Stable Image Platform</a> (CSIP), together with AMD Validated Server program, AMD True Server Solutions, AMD Thermally Tested Barebones Platforms and AMD Validated Server Program, providing certified systems for business from AMD.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Desktop_platforms">Desktop platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Desktop platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Starting in 2007, AMD, following Intel, began using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Codename" title="Codename">codenames</a> for its desktop platforms such as <i><a href="/wiki/AMD_Spider" title="AMD Spider">Spider</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/AMD_Dragon" title="AMD Dragon">Dragon</a></i>. The platforms, unlike Intel's approach, will refresh every year, putting focus on platform specialization. The platform includes components such as AMD processors, chipsets, ATI graphics and other features, but continued to the open platform approach, and welcome components from other vendors such as VIA, SiS, and Nvidia, as well as wireless product vendors.</p>
<p>Updates to the platform includes the implementation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOMMU" title="IOMMU">IOMMU</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Virtualization" title="AMD Virtualization">I/O Virtualization</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/45_nm" title="45 nm">45 nm</a> generation of processors, and the <a href="/wiki/AMD_800_chipset_series" title="AMD 800 chipset series">AMD 800 chipset series</a> in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_systems">Embedded systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Embedded systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alchemy_(processor)" title="Alchemy (processor)">Alchemy (processor)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geode_(processor)" title="Geode (processor)">Geode (processor)</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In February 2002, AMD acquired Alchemy Semiconductor for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alchemy_(processor)" title="Alchemy (processor)">Alchemy</a> line of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIPS_architecture" title="MIPS architecture">MIPS</a> processors for the hand-held and <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">portable media player</a> markets. On June 13, 2006, AMD officially announced that the line was to be transferred to Raza Microelectronics, Inc., a designer of MIPS processors for embedded applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alchemy_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alchemy-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2003, AMD also purchased the <a href="/wiki/Geode_(processor)" title="Geode (processor)">Geode</a> business which was originally the <a href="/wiki/Cyrix" title="Cyrix">Cyrix</a> <a href="/wiki/MediaGX" title="MediaGX">MediaGX</a> from <a href="/wiki/National_Semiconductor" title="National Semiconductor">National Semiconductor</a> to augment its existing line of embedded x86 processor products. During the second quarter of 2004, it launched new low-power Geode NX processors based on the K7 Thoroughbred architecture with speeds of fanless processors <span class="nowrap">667 MHz</span> and <span class="nowrap">1 GHz</span>, and <span class="nowrap">1.4 GHz</span> processor with fan, of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_Design_Power" title="Thermal Design Power">TDP</a> 25 W. This technology is used in a variety of embedded systems (Casino slot machines and customer kiosks for instance), several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra_Mobile_PC" title="Ultra Mobile PC">UMPC</a> designs in Asia markets, as well as the <a href="/wiki/One_Laptop_per_Child" title="One Laptop per Child">OLPC</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OLPC_XO-1" title="OLPC XO-1">XO-1 computer</a>, an inexpensive laptop computer intended to be distributed to children in developing countries around the world. The Geode LX processor was announced in 2005 and is said will continue to be available through 2015.</p>
<p>For the past couple of years AMD has been introducing <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">64-bit</a> processors into its embedded product line starting with the AMD <a href="/wiki/Opteron" title="Opteron">Opteron</a> processor. Leveraging the high throughput enabled through <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_Connect_Architecture" title="Direct Connect Architecture">Direct Connect Architecture</a> these server class processors have been targeted at high end telecom and storage applications. In 2007, AMD added the AMD Athlon, AMD Turion and Mobile AMD Sempron processors to its embedded product line. Leveraging the same <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">64-bit</a> instruction set and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_Connect_Architecture" title="Direct Connect Architecture">Direct Connect Architecture</a> as the AMD <a href="/wiki/Opteron" title="Opteron">Opteron</a> but at lower power levels, these processors were well suited to a variety of traditional embedded applications. Throughout 2007 and into 2008, AMD has continued to add both single-core Mobile AMD Sempron and AMD Athlon processors and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-core_(computing)" title="Multi-core (computing)">dual-core</a> AMD Athlon X2 and AMD Turion processors to its embedded product line and now offers embedded <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">64-bit</a> solutions starting with 8W TDP Mobile AMD Sempron and AMD Athlon processors for fan-less designs up to multi-processor systems leveraging multi-core AMD Opteron processors all supporting longer than standard availability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ATI acquisition included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imageon" title="Imageon">Imageon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xilleon" title="Xilleon">Xilleon</a> product lines. In late 2008, the entire handheld division was sold off to <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a>, who have since produced the <a href="/wiki/Adreno" title="Adreno">Adreno</a> series. The Xilleon division was sold to <a href="/wiki/Broadcom" title="Broadcom">Broadcom</a>.</p>
<p>In April 2007, AMD announced the release of the <a href="/wiki/AMD_690_chipset_series#M690T" title="AMD 690 chipset series">M690T</a> integrated graphics chipset for embedded designs. This enabled AMD to offer complete processor and chipset solutions targeted at embedded applications requiring high performance 3D and video such as emerging digital signage, kiosk and Point of Sale applications. The M690T was followed by the <a href="/wiki/AMD_690_chipset_series#M690E" title="AMD 690 chipset series">M690E</a> specifically for embedded applications which removed the TV output, which required <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macrovision" title="Macrovision">Macrovision</a> licensing for OEMs, and enabled native support for dual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transition_Minimized_Differential_Signaling" title="Transition Minimized Differential Signaling">TMDS</a> outputs, enabling dual independent <a href="/wiki/Digital_Visual_Interface" title="Digital Visual Interface">DVI</a> interfaces.</p>
<p>In 2008, AMD announced the Radeon E2400, the first discrete GPU in their embedded product line offering the same long term availability as their other embedded products. That was followed in 2009 with the higher performance Radeon E4690 discrete GPU.</p>
<p>In 2009, AMD announced their first BGA packaged e64 architecture processors, known as the ASB1 family.</p>
<p>In 2010, AMD announced a second generation BGA platform referred to as ASB2. They also announced several new AM3 based processors with support for DDR3 memory.</p>
<p>In January 2011, AMD announced the AMD Embedded G-Series <a href="/wiki/AMD_Accelerated_Processing_Unit" title="AMD Accelerated Processing Unit">Accelerated Processing Unit</a>. The first Fusion family APU for embedded applications. This announcement was followed by announcements for the high performance AMD Radeon E6760 and the value-conscious Radeon E6460 discrete GPUs. These solutions all added support for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DirectX_11" title="DirectX 11">DirectX 11</a>, <a href="/wiki/OpenGL" title="OpenGL">OpenGL</a> 4.1 and <a href="/wiki/OpenCL" title="OpenCL">OpenCL</a> 1.1.</p>
<p>In May 2012, AMD Announced the AMD Embedded R-Series<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R-Series_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-R-Series-137">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AMD_Accelerated_Processing_Unit" title="AMD Accelerated Processing Unit">Accelerated Processing Unit</a>. This family of products incorporates the Bulldozer CPU architecture, and Discrete-class AMD Radeon™ HD 7000G Series graphics.</p>
<p>AMD Embedded solutions offer 5+ year product life.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_graphics">Embedded graphics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Embedded graphics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>AMD builds graphic processors for use in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embedded_System" title="Embedded System">embedded</a> systems. These <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">SOCs</a> are used in a variety of applications and industries. They can be found in anything from casinos to healthcare, with a large portion of products being used in industrial machines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The latest E9000-Modules, based on the Polaris Microarchitecture, succeeded the previous E8000 series in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_initiatives">Other initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/50x15_(AMD)" title="50x15 (AMD)">50x15</a>, digital inclusion, with targeted 50% of world population to be connected through Internet via affordable computers by the year of 2015.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Green_Grid" title="The Green Grid">The Green Grid</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> founded by AMD together with other founders, such as <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, to seek lower power consumption for grids.</li>
<li>Codenamed <i>SIMFIRE</i> – interoperability testing tool for the Desktop and mobile Architecture for System Hardware (DASH) open architecture.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>AMD develops the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_CodeXL" title="AMD CodeXL">AMD CodeXL</a> tool suite which includes a GPU debugger, a GPU profiler, a CPU profiler and an OpenCL static kernel analyzer. CodeXL is freely available at AMD developer tools website.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Stream_SDK" title="AMD Stream SDK">AMD Stream SDK</a> and <a href="/wiki/AMD_APP_SDK" title="AMD APP SDK">AMD APP SDK</a> (Accelerated Parallel Processing) SDK to enable AMD graphics processing cores (GPU), working in concert with the system’s x86 cores (CPU), to execute heterogeneously to accelerate many applications beyond just graphics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></li>
<li>AMD has also taken an active part in developing <a href="/wiki/Coreboot" title="Coreboot">coreboot</a>, and open source projects aimed at replacing the proprietary BIOS firmware.</li>
<li>Other AMD software includes the <a href="/wiki/AMD_Core_Math_Library" title="AMD Core Math Library">AMD Core Math Library</a>, and open-source software including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_Performance_Library" title="AMD Performance Library">AMD Performance Library</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CodeAnalyst" title="CodeAnalyst">CodeAnalyst</a> performance profiler.</li>
<li>AMD contributes to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> projects, including working with <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a> to enhance <a href="/wiki/OpenSolaris" title="OpenSolaris">OpenSolaris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sun_xVM" title="Sun xVM">Sun xVM</a> on the AMD platform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> AMD also maintains its own <a href="/wiki/Open64" title="Open64">Open64</a> compiler distribution and contributes its changes back to the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>In 2008, AMD released the low-level programming specifications for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU">GPUs</a>, and works with the <a href="/wiki/X.Org_Foundation" title="X.Org Foundation">X.Org Foundation</a> to develop drivers for AMD graphics cards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Extensions for software parallelism (xSP), aimed at speeding up programs to enable multi-threaded and multi-core processing, announced in Technology Analyst Day 2007. One of the initiatives being discussed since August 2007 is the Light Weight <a href="/wiki/Profiling_(computer_programming)" title="Profiling (computer programming)">Profiling</a> (LWP), providing internal hardware monitor with runtimes, to observe information about executing process and help the re-design of software to be optimized with multi-core and even multi-threaded programs. Another one is the extension of Streaming SIMD Extension (SSE) instruction set, the <a href="/wiki/SSE5" title="SSE5">SSE5</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_and_fabrication">Production and fabrication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Production and fabrication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a></div>
<p>Ever since the spin-off of AMD's fabrication plants in early 2009, <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a> has been responsible for producing AMD's processors.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a>' main microprocessor manufacturing facilities are located in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, Germany. Additionally, highly integrated microprocessors are manufactured in Taiwan made by third-party manufacturers under strict license from AMD. Between 2003 and 2005, they constructed a second manufacturing plant (<span class="nowrap">300 mm</span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/90_nm" title="90 nm">90 nm</a> process <a href="/wiki/Silicon_on_insulator" title="Silicon on insulator">SOI</a>) in the same complex in order to increase the number of chips they could produce, thus becoming more competitive with <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>. The new plant was named "Fab 36", in recognition of AMD's 36 years of operation, and reached full production in mid-2007. Fab 36 was renamed to "Fab 1" during the spin-off of AMD's manufacturing business during the creation of <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a>. In July 2007, AMD announced that they completed the conversion of Fab 1 Module 1 from <span class="nowrap">90 nm</span> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/65_nm" title="65 nm">65 nm</a>. They then shifted their focus to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/45_nm" title="45 nm">45 nm</a> conversion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2016 <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> reported that AMD had successfully produced products on <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>'s <a href="/wiki/14_nanometer" title="14 nanometer">14 nanometer</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FinFET" title="FinFET">FinFET</a> process. This presents additional manufacturing opportunities, in addition to AMD's primary foundries: GlobalFoundries and <a href="/wiki/TSMC" title="TSMC">TSMC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> It was argued this would reduce risk for AMD by decreasing dependence on any one foundry.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>AMD utilizes strategic industry partnerships to further its business interests as well as to rival Intel's dominance and resources.</p>
<p>A partnership between AMD and Alpha Processor Inc. developed <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a>, a point-to-point interconnect standard which was turned over to an industry standards body for finalization. It is now used in modern motherboards that are compatible with AMD processors.</p>
<p>AMD also formed a strategic partnership with IBM, under which AMD gained <a href="/wiki/Silicon_on_insulator" title="Silicon on insulator">silicon on insulator</a> (SOI) manufacturing technology, and detailed advice on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/90_nm" title="90 nm">90 nm</a> implementation. AMD announced that the partnership would extend to 2011 for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/32_nm" title="32 nm">32 nm</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/22_nm" title="22 nm">22 nm</a> fabrication-related technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>To facilitate processor distribution and sales, AMD is loosely partnered with end-user companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">HP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Compaq" title="Compaq">Compaq</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASUS" title="ASUS">ASUS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acer_(company)" title="Acer (company)">Acer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a>.</p>
<p>In 1993, AMD established a 50-50 partnership with <a href="/wiki/Fujitsu" title="Fujitsu">Fujitsu</a> called FASL, and merged into a new company called FASL LLC in 2003. The joint venture went public under the name <a href="/wiki/Spansion" title="Spansion">Spansion</a> and ticker symbol SPSN in December 2005, with AMD shares drop to 37%. AMD no longer directly participates in the Flash memory devices market now as AMD entered into a non-competition agreement, as of December 21, 2005, with Fujitsu and Spansion, pursuant to which it agreed not to directly or indirectly engage in a business that manufactures or supplies standalone semiconductor devices (including single chip, multiple chip or system devices) containing only Flash memory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 18, 2006, Dell announced that it would roll out new servers based on AMD's Opteron chips by year's end, thus ending an exclusive relationship with Intel. In September 2006, Dell began offering AMD Athlon X2 chips in their desktop line-up.</p>
<p>In June 2011, HP announced new business and consumer notebooks equipped with the latest versions of AMD APUs – accelerated processing units. AMD will power HP's Intel-based business notebooks as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the spring of 2013, AMD announced that it would be powering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(eighth_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (eighth generation)">all three major next-generation consoles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> are both powered by a custom-built AMD APU, and the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> is powered by an AMD GPU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> According to AMD, having their processors in all three of these consoles will greatly assist developers with cross-platform development to competing consoles and PCs as well as increased support for their products across the board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>AMD has entered into an MoU with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hindustan_Semiconductor_Manufacturing_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hindustan Semiconductor Manufacturing Corporation (page does not exist)">Hindustan Semiconductor Manufacturing Corporation(HSMC)</a> to explore various options for providing technology licence to manufacture micro-processors in the semi conductor fabs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation_with_Intel">Litigation with Intel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Litigation with Intel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD_v._Intel" title="AMD v. Intel">AMD v. Intel</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amd_386_processor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2355" data-file-width="3528" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amd_386_processor.jpg/220px-Amd_386_processor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amd_386_processor.jpg/330px-Amd_386_processor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Amd_386_processor.jpg/440px-Amd_386_processor.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amd_386_processor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
AMD processor with Intel logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>AMD has a long history of litigation with former partner and x86 creator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" title="Intel Corporation">Intel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-litigation_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-litigation-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>In 1986, Intel broke an agreement it had with AMD to allow them to produce Intel's micro-chips for <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>; AMD filed for <a href="/wiki/Arbitration" title="Arbitration">arbitration</a> in 1987 and the arbitrator decided in AMD's favor in 1992. Intel disputed this, and the case ended up in the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a>. In 1994, that court upheld the arbitrator's decision and awarded damages for breach of contract.</li>
<li>In 1990, Intel brought a copyright infringement action alleging illegal use of its 287 microcode. The case ended in 1994 with a jury finding for AMD and its right to use Intel's microcode in its microprocessors through the 486 generation.</li>
<li>In 1997, Intel filed suit against AMD and <a href="/wiki/Cyrix" title="Cyrix">Cyrix</a> Corp. for misuse of the term <a href="/wiki/MMX_(instruction_set)" title="MMX (instruction set)">MMX</a>. AMD and Intel settled, with AMD acknowledging MMX as a trademark owned by Intel, and with Intel granting AMD rights to market the AMD K6 MMX processor.</li>
<li>In 2005, following an investigation, the Japan Federal Trade Commission found Intel guilty on a number of violations. On June 27, 2005, AMD won an <a href="/wiki/United_States_antitrust_law" title="United States antitrust law">antitrust</a> suit against Intel in Japan, and on the same day, AMD filed a broad antitrust complaint against Intel in the U.S. Federal District Court in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>. The complaint alleges systematic use of secret rebates, special discounts, threats, and other means used by Intel to lock AMD processors out of the global market. Since the start of this action, the court has issued <a href="/wiki/Subpoena" title="Subpoena">subpoenas</a> to major computer manufacturers including <a href="/wiki/Acer_Inc." title="Acer Inc.">Acer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenovo" title="Lenovo">Lenovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">HP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a>.</li>
<li>In November 2009, Intel agreed to pay AMD $1.25bn and renew a five-year patent cross-licensing agreement as part of a deal to settle all outstanding legal disputes between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amd_suit_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-amd_suit-172">[172]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guinness_World_Record_Achievement">Guinness World Record Achievement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Guinness World Record Achievement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 31, 2011, in Austin, Texas, AMD achieved a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Record</a> for the "Highest frequency of a computer processor": 8.429 GHz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Record-173">[173]</a></sup> The company ran an 8-core FX-8150 processor with only one active module (two cores), and cooled with liquid helium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtube-174">[174]</a></sup> The previous record was 8.308 GHz, with an Intel Celeron 352 (one core).</p>
<p>On November 1, 2011, geek.com reported that Andre Yang, an <a href="/wiki/Overclocking" title="Overclocking">overclocker</a> from Taiwan, used an FX-8150 to set another record: 8.461 GHz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record2_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-record2-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 19, 2012, Andre Yang used an FX-8350 to set another record yet again: 8794.33MHz (8.794GHz).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_social_responsibility">Corporate social responsibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Corporate social responsibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In its 2012 report on progress relating to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_minerals" title="Conflict minerals">conflict minerals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Enough_Project" title="Enough Project">Enough Project</a> rated AMD the fifth most progressive of 24 consumer electronics companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnoughProject2012_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnoughProject2012-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Micro_Devices&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-118">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jeffrey Burt, eWeek. "<a class="external text" href="http://www.eweek.com/c/a/Desktops-and-Notebooks/AMD-Cuts-Q3-Forecast-Due-to-Chip-Manufacturing-Problems-581901/" rel="nofollow">AMD Cuts Q3 Forecast Due to Chip Manufacturing Problems</a>". September 28, 2011. Retrieved October 7, 2011. More AMD APUs for laptops running Windows 7 and Windows 8 OS are being used commonly. These include AMD's price-point APUs, the E1 and E2, and their mainstream competitors with Intel's core i-series: The Vision A- series, the A standing for accelerated. These range from the lower-performance A4 chipset to the A6, A8, and A10. These all incorporate Next-generation Radeon graphics cards, with the A4 utilizing the base Radeon HD chip and the rest using a Radeon R4 graphics card, with the exception of the highest-model A10 (A10-7300) which uses an R6 graphics card.</span></li>
